until\\n241:      * authentication succeeds or fails.\\n242:      *\\n243:      * The messages are sent and received as size delimited bytes that consists of a 4 byte network-ordered size N\\n244:      * followed by N bytes representing the opaque payload.\\n245:      */\\n246:     @SuppressWarnings(\\\"fallthrough\\\")\\n247:     @Override\\n248:     public void authenticate() throws IOException {\\n249:         if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\\n250:             if (netOutBuffer != null && !flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps())\\n251:                 return;\\n252: \\n253:             if (saslServer != null && saslServer.isComplete()) {\\n254:                 setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\\n255:                 return;\\n256:             }\\n257: \\n258: connectionId);\\n260: \\n261:             try {\\n262:                 netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);\\n263:             } catch (InvalidReceiveException e) {\\n264:                 throw new      break;\\n285:                     // For default GSSAPI, fall through to authenticate using the client token as the first GSSAPI packet.\\n286:                     // This is required for interoperability with 0.9.0.x clients which do not send handshake request\\n287:                 case AUTHENTICATE:\\n288:                     handleSaslToken(clientToken);\\n289:                     // When the authentication exchange is complete and no more tokens are expected from the client,\\n290:                     // update SASL state. }\\n335: \\n336:     @Override\\n337:     public void close() throws IOException {\\n338:         if (principalBuilder instanceof Closeable)\\n339:             Utils.closeQuietly((Closeable) KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\\n442:             RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\\n443: // This should not normally occur since clients typically check supported versions using ApiVersionsRequest\\n451:                 throw new UnsupportedVersionException(\\\"Version \\\" + version + \\n504:     private boolean handleKafkaRequest(byte[] requestBytes) throws IOException, AuthenticationException {\\n505:         boolean isKafkaRequest = false;\\n506:         String clientMechanism = null;\\n507:         try {\\n508:             ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(requestBytes);\\n509:             RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\\n510:             ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\\n511: \\n512:             // A valid Kafka request header was received. This avoids\\n519:             // unnecessary exposure to some of the more complex schema types.\\n520:             if (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\\n521:                 throw new IllegalSaslStateException(\\\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \\\" + apiKey + \\\" during SASL handshake.\\\");\\n522: \\n523:             LOG.debug(\\\"Handling Kafka request {} during {}\\\", apiKey, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\\n524: \\n525: \\n526:             RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\\n527:                     KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\\n528:             RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\\n529:             if (apiKey == ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS)\\n530:                 handleApiVersionsRequest(requestContext, (ApiVersionsRequest) requestAndSize.request);\\n531:             else\\n532:                 clientMechanism = handleHandshakeRequest(requestContext, (SaslHandshakeRequest) requestAndSize.request);\\n533:         } catch (InvalidRequestException e) {\\n534:             if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST) {\\n535:                 // InvalidRequestException is thrown if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key\\n536:                 // is invalid. (LOG.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n539:                     StringBuilder tokenBuilder = new StringBuilder();\\n540:                     for (byte b : requestBytes) {\\n541:                         tokenBuilder.append(String.format(\\\"%02x\\\", b));\\n542:                         if (tokenBuilder.length() >= 20)\\n543:                              break;\\n544:                     }\\n545:                     LOG.debug(\\\"Received client packet of length {} starting with bytes 0x{}, process as GSSAPI packet\\\", requestBytes.length, tokenBuilder);\\n546:                 }\\n547: UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\\\"Exception handling first SASL packet from client, GSSAPI is not supported by server\\\", e);\\n552:             } else\\n553:                 throw e;\\n554: handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\\n564:         String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\\n565:         short version = context.header.apiVersion();\\n566:         if (version >= 1)\\n567:             this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(true);\\n568:         if (enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)) {\\n569:             LOG.debug(\\\"Using SASL mechanism '{}' provided by client\\\", The authorization flow checks whether ACLs exist and applies the appropriate rules based on the configuration and deny/allow lists.\n\nThe core authorization logic evaluates access by checking if either no ACLs exist with a permissive configuration, or if there's no DENY ACL paired with an ALLOW ACL. I need to examine the `matchingAcls()` function more closely to see how it filters resources, as this is critical to ensuring the right ACLs are being evaluated.\n\nThe function retrieves ACLs from a cache snapshot using three matching strategies: exact literal matches on the resource name, wildcard patterns, and prefix-based patterns. It constructs an `AclSeqs` object containing prefixed ACLs, wildcard ACLs, and literal ACLs separately, which suggests the authorization logic later evaluates these different categories in a specific order.\n\nHowever, there's a logical problem with the range query for prefix matching. The `from()` call starts at the full resource name with `PREFIXED` pattern type, while `to()` ends at just the first character of that name. This creates a backwards range—for example, with \"topic123\", it tries to query from \"topic123\" down to \"t\". Since SortedMap range queries expect the \"from\" key to be less than or equal to the \"to\" key, this range would be empty or behave unexpectedly depending on how the ResourceOrdering comparator handles this scenario. b.name) * -1`, then \"t\" comes before \"topic123\" in the sorted order, making `from(\"topic123\") to(\"t\")` an empty range.\n\nThe range query is fundamentally broken. When comparing \"topic123\" to \"t\", the first character matches but \"topic123\" is longer, so it's lexicographically greater. With the reverse comparator, this means \"topic123\" appears before \"t\" in iteration order. Calling `from(\"topic123\")` gets entries >= \"topic123\", but `to(\"t\")` gets entries < \"t\", which excludes everything between them since the ordering is inverted. This means the prefixed ACL lookup returns nothing. The first element via iterator is the lexicographically largest string, and the last is the smallest. Since `resourceName.take(1)` extracts just the first character, for \"topic123\" this gives \"t\". In the reversed ordering, \"topic123\" comes before \"t\" because it's lexicographically larger. The range from `from(\"topic123\")` to `to(\"t\")` would be empty—`from(\"topic123\")` includes everything >= \"topic123\" in reversed order, while `to(\"t\")` includes everything < \"t\" in reversed order, and since \"t\" is actually greater than \"topic123\" lexicographically, it falls before \"topic123\" in the reversed ordering.\n\nThis appears to be a bug. The code intends to retrieve all prefixed ACLs that match prefixes of the resource name—so for \"topic123\", it should find patterns like \"t\", \"to\", \"top\", etc. However, the reversed ordering causes the range query to return nothing.
